 1938: 
 1939: =head2 sending_software()
 1940: 
 1941: Returns information extracted from headers that identify the software or
 1942: server-side infrastructure used to compose or inject the message.  These
 1943: headers are injected by email clients, bulk-mailing libraries, and shared
 1944: hosting control panels, and are often the most direct evidence of how the
 1945: spam was sent and from which server.
 1946: 
 1947: Headers examined: C<X-Mailer>, C<User-Agent>, C<X-PHP-Originating-Script>,
 1948: C<X-Source>, C<X-Source-Args>, C<X-Source-Host>.
 1949: 
 1950: The C<X-PHP-Originating-Script>, C<X-Source>, and C<X-Source-Host> headers
 1951: in particular are injected automatically by many shared hosting providers
 1952: (cPanel, Plesk, DirectAdmin) and reveal the exact PHP script path and
 1953: hostname responsible.  A hosting abuse team can use these values to
 1954: identify the compromised or malicious account immediately, without needing
 1955: to search logs.
 1956: 
 1957: The data is extracted synchronously during C<parse_email()> with no network
 1958: I/O.  This method simply returns the pre-built list.
 1959: 
 1960: =head3 Usage
 1961: 
 1962:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 1963:     my @sw = $analyser->sending_software();
 1964: 
 1965:     for my $s (@sw) {
 1966:         printf "%-30s : %s\n", $s->{header}, $s->{value};
 1967:         printf "  Note: %s\n", $s->{note};
 1968:     }
 1969: 
 1970:     # Check for shared-hosting injection headers
 1971:     my @hosting = grep {
 1972:         $_->{header} =~ /^x-(?:php-originating-script|source)/
 1973:     } @sw;
 1974: 
 1975:     if (@hosting) {
 1976:         print "Shared-hosting script detected -- report to hosting abuse team:\n";
 1977:         print "  $_->{header}: $_->{value}\n" for @hosting;
 1978:     }
 1979: 
 1980:     # Extract the mailer name if present
 1981:     my ($mailer) = grep { $_->{header} eq 'x-mailer' } @sw;
 1982:     printf "Sent with: %s\n", $mailer->{value} if $mailer;
 1983: 
 1984: =head3 Arguments
 1985: 
 1986: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 1987: 
 1988: =head3 Returns
 1989: 
 1990: A list (not an arrayref) of hashrefs, one per recognised software-fingerprint
 1991: header that was present in the message, in alphabetical order of header name.
 1992: Returns an empty list if none of the watched headers are present, or if
 1993: C<parse_email()> has not been called.
 1994: 
 1995:     {
 1996:         header => 'X-PHP-Originating-Script',
 1997:         value  => '1000:newsletter.php',
 1998:         note   => 'PHP script on shared hosting - report to hosting abuse team',
 1999:     }
 2000: 
 2001: Each hashref contains exactly three keys, all always present:
 2002: 
 2003: =over 4
 2004: 
 2005: =item C<header> (string)
 2006: 
 2007: The header name, lower-cased.  One of the six values listed in the
 2008: Algorithm section below.
 2009: 
 2010: =item C<value> (string)
 2011: 
 2012: The header value exactly as it appeared in the message (not decoded or
 2013: transformed in any way).
 2014: 
 2015: =item C<note> (string)
 2016: 
 2017: A fixed, human-readable annotation describing what this header represents
 2018: and the recommended action.  The note string is determined by the header
 2019: name and is the same for all messages; it is not derived from the value.
 2020: See the Algorithm section for the note associated with each header.
 2021: 
 2022: =back
 2023: 
 2024: =head3 Side Effects
 2025: 
 2026: None.  All data is collected during C<parse_email()> and this method
 2027: only returns the pre-collected list.  No network I/O is performed.
 2028: 
 2029: =head3 Algorithm: headers examined
 2030: 
 2031: The following six headers are examined during C<parse_email()>.  They are
 2032: checked in alphabetical order; the result list preserves that order
 2033: (i.e. C<user-agent> appears before C<x-mailer> which appears before
 2034: C<x-php-originating-script>, etc.).  At most one entry per header name is
 2035: produced even if the header appears more than once; the first occurrence is
 2036: used.
 2037: 
 2038: =over 4
 2039: 
 2040: =item C<user-agent>
 2041: 
 2042: Note: C<"Email client identifier">
 2043: 
 2044: Set by some email clients (Thunderbird, Evolution) as an alternative to
 2045: C<X-Mailer>.  Identifies the application that composed the message.
 2046: 
 2047: =item C<x-mailer>
 2048: 
 2049: Note: C<"Email client or bulk-mailer identifier">
 2050: 
 2051: The most widely used header for identifying the sending application.
 2052: Values range from standard clients (C<"Apple Mail">, C<"Microsoft Outlook">)
 2053: to bulk-mailing libraries (C<"PHPMailer 6.0">, C<"MailMate">).  Its presence
 2054: in spam often reveals the library used to generate the campaign.
 2055: 
 2056: =item C<x-php-originating-script>
 2057: 
 2058: Note: C<"PHP script on shared hosting -- report to hosting abuse team">
 2059: 
 2060: Injected by cPanel and similar shared-hosting control panels when a PHP
 2061: script sends mail via the local MTA.  The value typically takes the form
 2062: C<uid:script.php> (e.g. C<"1000:newsletter.php">), directly identifying
 2063: the Unix user account and the script responsible.  This is the single most
 2064: actionable header for shared-hosting abuse reports.
 2065: 
 2066: =item C<x-source>
 2067: 
 2068: Note: C<"Source file on shared hosting -- report to hosting abuse team">
 2069: 
 2070: Also injected by shared-hosting platforms, typically containing the full
 2071: filesystem path to the sending script (e.g.
 2072: C<"/home/user/public_html/contact.php">).  Complements
 2073: C<X-PHP-Originating-Script>.
 2074: 
 2075: =item C<x-source-args>
 2076: 
 2077: Note: C<"Command-line args injected by shared hosting provider">
 2078: 
 2079: The command-line arguments of the process that sent the mail, injected by
 2080: some hosting platforms.  May reveal interpreter invocations or script
 2081: parameters useful for forensic analysis.
 2082: 
 2083: =item C<x-source-host>
 2084: 
 2085: Note: C<"Sending hostname injected by shared hosting provider">
 2086: 
 2087: The hostname of the server that submitted the message, injected by the
 2088: hosting platform.  Useful when the IP in the C<Received:> chain is a shared
 2089: outbound relay rather than the originating server.
 2090: 
 2091: =back
 2092: 
 2093: =head3 Notes
 2094: 
 2095: =over 4
 2096: 
 2097: =item *
 2098: 
 2099: The result list is reset to empty by each call to C<parse_email()>.  If no
 2100: watched headers are present in the current message, the list is empty.
 2101: 
 2102: =item *
 2103: 
 2104: The alphabetical ordering of entries is a side effect of iterating over
 2105: the C<%sw_notes> hash in sorted key order.  It is stable across calls on
 2106: the same message.
 2107: 
 2108: =item *
 2109: 
 2110: Header names are stored lower-cased (e.g. C<'x-mailer'>, not C<'X-Mailer'>).
 2111: Header values are stored verbatim, preserving the original case and
 2112: whitespace.
 2113: 
 2114: =item *
 2115: 
 2116: The C<note> field is a fixed annotation string chosen by the module, not
 2117: text extracted from the message.  It is safe to display directly in reports
 2118: without sanitisation.
 2119: 
 2120: =item *
 2121: 
 2122: If both C<X-PHP-Originating-Script> and C<X-Source> are present (common on
 2123: cPanel systems), both are returned as separate list entries.  A caller
 2124: building a hosting abuse report should include all entries whose C<header>
 2125: begins with C<x->.
 2126: 
 2127: =back
 2128: 
 2129: =head3 API Specification
 2130: 
 2131: =head4 Input
 2132: 
 2133:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 2134:     # No arguments.
 2135:     []
 2136: 
 2137: =head4 Output
 2138: 
 2139:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 2140: 
 2141:     # A list (possibly empty) of hashrefs, in alphabetical header-name order:
 2142:     (
 2143:         {
 2144:             type => HASHREF,
 2145:             keys => {
 2146:                 header => {
 2147:                     type  => SCALAR,
 2148:                     regex => qr/^(?:user-agent|x-mailer|x-php-originating-script
 2149:                                    |x-source|x-source-args|x-source-host)$/x,
 2150:                 },
 2151:                 value => {
 2152:                     type => SCALAR,
 2153:                     # Verbatim header value; may be any non-empty string.
 2154:                 },
 2155:                 note => {
 2156:                     type  => SCALAR,
 2157:                     # Fixed annotation string; one of the six strings
 2158:                     # documented in the Algorithm section above.
 2159:                 },
 2160:             },
 2161:         },
 2162:         # ... one hashref per recognised header present, alphabetical order
 2163:     )
 2164: 
 2165:     # Empty list when none of the six watched headers are present.
 2166: 
 2167: =cut
 2168: 
 2169: sub sending_software {
 2170: 	my $self = $_[0];
 2171: 
 2172: 	return @{ $self->{_sending_sw} };
 2173: }
 2174: 
 2175: 
 2176: =head2 received_trail()
 2177: 
 2178: Returns the per-hop tracking data extracted from the C<Received:> header
 2179: chain: the IP address, envelope recipient address, and server-assigned
 2180: session ID for each relay that handled the message.
 2181: 
 2182: When filing an abuse report with a transit ISP or relay operator, these
 2183: are the identifiers their postmaster team needs to look up the specific
 2184: SMTP session in their mail logs.  Without the session ID or envelope
 2185: recipient, an ISP typically cannot locate a single message among billions
 2186: of log entries; with them, the lookup takes seconds.
 2187: 
 2188: The data is extracted synchronously during C<parse_email()> with no network
 2189: I/O.  This method simply returns the pre-built list.
 2190: 
 2191: =head3 Usage
 2192: 
 2193:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 2194:     my @trail = $analyser->received_trail();
 2195: 
 2196:     for my $hop (@trail) {
 2197:         printf "Hop IP : %s\n",  $hop->{ip}       // '(unknown)';
 2198:         printf "  For  : %s\n",  $hop->{for}       if defined $hop->{for};
 2199:         printf "  ID   : %s\n",  $hop->{id}        if defined $hop->{id};
 2200:         printf "  Raw  : %s\n",  $hop->{received};
 2201:         print  "\n";
 2202:     }
 2203: 
 2204:     # Build a list of session IDs to include in an abuse report
 2205:     my @ids = map  { "$_->{ip}: id $_->{id}" }
 2206:               grep { defined $_->{id} }
 2207:               @trail;
 2208: 
 2209:     # Find which ISP handled a particular relay IP
 2210:     my ($hop) = grep { ($_->{ip} // '') eq '91.198.174.5' } @trail;
 2211:     if ($hop) {
 2212:         print "Session ID at that relay: $hop->{id}\n" if defined $hop->{id};
 2213:     }
 2214: 
 2215: =head3 Arguments
 2216: 
 2217: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 2218: 
 2219: =head3 Returns
 2220: 
 2221: A list (not an arrayref) of hashrefs, one per C<Received:> hop from which
 2222: at least one of an IP address, an envelope recipient address, or a server
 2223: session ID could be extracted, in oldest-first order (i.e. the first element
 2224: is the outermost relay, the last element is the most recent hop before your
 2225: own server).  Returns an empty list if no C<Received:> headers are present
 2226: or none yielded any extractable data, or if C<parse_email()> has not been
 2227: called.
 2228: 
 2229:     (
 2230:       { received => '...raw header...', ip => '1.2.3.4',
 2231:         for => 'victim@example.com', id => 'ABC123' },
 2232:       ...
 2233:     )
 2234: 
 2235: Each hashref contains exactly four keys:
 2236: 
 2237: =over 4
 2238: 
 2239: =item C<received> (string, always present)
 2240: 
 2241: The complete raw value of the C<Received:> header for this hop, exactly as
 2242: it appeared in the message.  Suitable for including verbatim in an abuse
 2243: report so the receiving ISP can see the full context.
 2244: 
 2245: =item C<ip> (string or undef)
 2246: 
 2247: The IPv4 address extracted from this C<Received:> hop, or C<undef> if no
 2248: recognisable IPv4 address was found.  Uses the same four-pattern extraction
 2249: priority as C<originating_ip()>: bracketed C<[1.2.3.4]> first, then
 2250: parenthesised, then C<from hostname addr>, then any bare dotted-quad as a
 2251: last resort.  Private, reserved, and trusted IPs are B<not> filtered here;
 2252: all IPs including RFC 1918 addresses are returned as found.  (Filtering is
 2253: applied only by C<originating_ip()>.)
 2254: 
 2255: =item C<for> (string or undef)
 2256: 
 2257: The envelope recipient address extracted from the C<for> clause of the
 2258: C<Received:> header (e.g. C<for E<lt>victim@example.comE<gt>>), or C<undef>
 2259: if no such clause is present or it does not contain a fully-qualified email
 2260: address (one with both a local part and a domain containing at least one
 2261: dot).  Bare postmaster addresses, C<for multiple recipients>, and similar
 2262: non-address forms are not captured and result in C<undef>.
 2263: 
 2264: =item C<id> (string or undef)
 2265: 
 2266: The server's internal session or queue identifier from the C<id> clause
 2267: of the C<Received:> header (e.g. C<with ESMTP id ABC123XYZ>), or C<undef>
 2268: if no C<id> clause is present.  The value is a single whitespace-delimited
 2269: token of word characters and dots; longer or more structured ID formats may
 2270: be truncated at the first whitespace boundary.
 2271: 
 2272: =back
 2273: 
 2274: =head3 Side Effects
 2275: 
 2276: None.  All data is collected during C<parse_email()> and this method only
 2277: returns the pre-collected list.  No network I/O is performed.
 2278: 
 2279: =head3 Algorithm: extraction and ordering
 2280: 
 2281: During C<parse_email()>, the C<Received:> headers are walked in reverse
 2282: message order (i.e. oldest hop first, which is the same order as
 2283: C<originating_ip()>'s chain walk).  For each header:
 2284: 
 2285: =over 4
 2286: 
 2287: =item 1.
 2288: 
 2289: The IP address is extracted using the same four-pattern priority sequence
 2290: documented in C<originating_ip()>.
 2291: 
 2292: =item 2.
 2293: 
 2294: The envelope recipient is extracted with the pattern
 2295: C<\bfor\s+E<lt>?([^\s>]+@[\w.-]+\.[\w]+)E<gt>?> (case-insensitive).  The
 2296: domain portion of the address must contain at least one dot; single-label
 2297: names such as C<postmaster> are not matched.
 2298: 
 2299: =item 3.
 2300: 
 2301: The session ID is extracted with the pattern C<\bid\s+([\w.-]+)>
 2302: (case-insensitive), capturing the first word-character token following the
 2303: keyword C<id>.
 2304: 
 2305: =item 4.
 2306: 
 2307: If none of the three fields can be extracted (all are C<undef>), the hop is
 2308: silently discarded and does not appear in the result list.  This suppresses
 2309: internal or synthetic hops that carry no useful tracking information.
 2310: 
 2311: =back
 2312: 
 2313: The result list therefore contains only hops that carry at least one
 2314: actionable piece of tracking data.
 2315: 
 2316: =head3 Notes
 2317: 
 2318: =over 4
 2319: 
 2320: =item *
 2321: 
 2322: The result list is reset to empty by each call to C<parse_email()>.  It
 2323: reflects the C<Received:> headers of the current message only.
 2324: 
 2325: =item *
 2326: 
 2327: Oldest-first ordering means C<$trail[0]> is the first relay the message
 2328: passed through after leaving the sender, and C<$trail[-1]> is the last hop
 2329: before your own server.  This is the natural order for walking the chain
 2330: when composing a forwarded abuse report.
 2331: 
 2332: =item *
 2333: 
 2334: C<ip> may be C<undef> for a hop that nonetheless has a valid C<for> or
 2335: C<id> field -- for example, a C<Received:> header added by a local
 2336: delivery agent that does not record an IP.  Always test C<defined
 2337: $hop-E<gt>{ip}> before using it.
 2338: 
 2339: =item *
 2340: 
 2341: C<for> and C<id> are C<undef>, not the empty string, when absent.  C<ip>
 2342: is also C<undef>, not C<'(unknown)'> as in some other methods.  All four
 2343: fields must be tested with C<defined>, not boolean truthiness, to
 2344: distinguish between absent and empty.
 2345: 
 2346: =item *
 2347: 
 2348: C<report()> applies an additional filter when displaying this data: it only
 2349: shows hops where C<id> or C<for> is defined, suppressing hops where only
 2350: an IP was found.  C<received_trail()> itself returns all hops with any
 2351: extractable data, including IP-only hops, giving callers the full picture.
 2352: 
 2353: =item *
 2354: 
 2355: The C<received> field is the unfolded header value as stored after RFC 2822
 2356: line-folding is removed during C<parse_email()>.  Continuation whitespace
 2357: is replaced with a single space; the value will not contain embedded
 2358: newlines.
 2359: 
 2360: =back
 2361: 
 2362: =head3 API Specification
 2363: 
 2364: =head4 Input
 2365: 
 2366:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 2367:     # No arguments.
 2368:     []
 2369: 
 2370: =head4 Output
 2371: 
 2372:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 2373: 
 2374:     # A list (possibly empty) of hashrefs, oldest-hop first:
 2375:     (
 2376:         {
 2377:             type => HASHREF,
 2378:             keys => {
 2379:                 received => {
 2380:                     type => SCALAR,
 2381:                     # Complete unfolded Received: header value; always defined.
 2382:                 },
 2383:                 ip => {
 2384:                     type     => SCALAR,
 2385:                     optional => 1,  # present but may be undef
 2386:                     regex    => qr/^\d{1,3}(?:\.\d{1,3}){3}$/,
 2387:                 },
 2388:                 for => {
 2389:                     type     => SCALAR,
 2390:                     optional => 1,  # present but may be undef
 2391:                     # Fully-qualified email address: local@domain.tld
 2392:                     regex    => qr/^[^\s@]+\@[\w.-]+\.[a-zA-Z]{2,}$/,
 2393:                 },
 2394:                 id => {
 2395:                     type     => SCALAR,
 2396:                     optional => 1,  # present but may be undef
 2397:                     regex    => qr/^[\w.-]+$/,
 2398:                 },
 2399:             },
 2400:         },
 2401:         # ... one hashref per hop with at least one extractable field,
 2402:         #     in oldest-first (outermost relay first) order
 2403:     )
 2404: 
 2405:     # Empty list when no Received: headers are present or none yielded
 2406:     # any extractable data.
 2407: 
 2408: =cut
 2409: 
 2410: sub received_trail {
 2411: 	my $self = $_[0];
 2412: 
 2413: 	return @{ $self->{_rcvd_tracking} };
 2414: }
 2415: 
 2416: =head2 risk_assessment()
 2417: 
 2418: Evaluates the message against a set of heuristic checks and returns an
 2419: overall risk level, a weighted numeric score, and a list of every specific
 2420: red flag that contributed to the score.
 2421: 
 2422: The assessment covers five categories: originating IP characteristics, email
 2423: authentication results, C<Date:> header validity, identity and header
 2424: consistency, and URL and domain properties.  Each finding is assigned a
 2425: severity, a machine-readable flag name, and a human-readable detail string.
 2426: 
 2427: The result is computed once and cached; subsequent calls on the same object
 2428: return the same hashref without repeating any analysis.  Calling
 2429: C<risk_assessment()> also implicitly triggers C<originating_ip()>,
 2430: C<embedded_urls()>, and C<mailto_domains()> if they have not already been
 2431: called, performing all associated network I/O.
 2432: 
 2433: =head3 Usage
 2434: 
 2435:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 2436:     my $risk = $analyser->risk_assessment();
 2437: 
 2438:     printf "Risk level : %s (score: %d)\n", $risk->{level}, $risk->{score};
 2439: 
 2440:     for my $f (@{ $risk->{flags} }) {
 2441:         printf "  [%-6s] %s\n    %s\n",
 2442:             $f->{severity}, $f->{flag}, $f->{detail};
 2443:     }
 2444: 
 2445:     # Gate an automated report on HIGH level only
 2446:     if ($risk->{level} eq 'HIGH') {
 2447:         send_abuse_report($analyser->abuse_report_text());
 2448:     }
 2449: 
 2450:     # Collect only HIGH and MEDIUM flags for a summary
 2451:     my @significant = grep { $_->{severity} =~ /^(?:HIGH|MEDIUM)$/ }
 2452:                       @{ $risk->{flags} };
 2453: 
 2454:     # Check for a specific flag
 2455:     my ($flag) = grep { $_->{flag} eq 'recently_registered_domain' }
 2456:                  @{ $risk->{flags} };
 2457:     warn "Phishing domain suspected\n" if $flag;
 2458: 
 2459:     # INFO level means no actionable red flags
 2460:     if ($risk->{level} eq 'INFO') {
 2461:         print "No significant red flags detected.\n";
 2462:     }
 2463: 
 2464: =head3 Arguments
 2465: 
 2466: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 2467: 
 2468: =head3 Returns
 2469: 
 2470: Returns a hashref with an overall risk level and a list of specific
 2471: red flags found in the message:
 2472: 
 2473:     {
 2474:         level => 'HIGH',          # HIGH | MEDIUM | LOW | INFO
 2475:         score => 7,               # raw weighted score
 2476:         flags => [
 2477:             { severity => 'HIGH',   flag => 'recently_registered_domain',
 2478:               detail => 'firmluminary.com registered 2025-09-01 (< 180 days ago)' },
 2479:             { severity => 'MEDIUM', flag => 'residential_sending_ip',
 2480:               detail => 'rDNS 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au looks like a broadband line' },
 2481:             { severity => 'MEDIUM', flag => 'url_shortener',
 2482:               detail => 'bit.ly used - real destination hidden' },
 2483:             ...
 2484:         ],
 2485:     }
 2486: 
 2487: A hashref with exactly three keys, all always present:
 2488: 
 2489: =over 4
 2490: 
 2491: =item C<level> (string)
 2492: 
 2493: The overall risk classification, determined by the weighted score:
 2494: 
 2495:     Score >= 9  =>  'HIGH'
 2496:     Score >= 5  =>  'MEDIUM'
 2497:     Score >= 2  =>  'LOW'
 2498:     Score <  2  =>  'INFO'
 2499: 
 2500: C<'INFO'> means either no flags were raised or only zero-weight (INFO
 2501: severity) flags were raised.  It does not mean the message is definitely
 2502: legitimate; it means no significant heuristic evidence of spam was found.
 2503: 
 2504: =item C<score> (integer)
 2505: 
 2506: The sum of the weights of all flags raised.  Weights by severity:
 2507: 
 2508:     HIGH   => 3
 2509:     MEDIUM => 2
 2510:     LOW    => 1
 2511:     INFO   => 0
 2512: 
 2513: The score is a non-negative integer.  Multiple flags of the same severity
 2514: each contribute their full weight independently; there is no cap on the
 2515: score.
 2516: 
 2517: =item C<flags> (arrayref of hashrefs)
 2518: 
 2519: A reference to a list of flag hashrefs, one per red flag raised, in the
 2520: order they were detected.  Each hashref contains exactly three keys:
 2521: 
 2522: =over 8
 2523: 
 2524: =item C<severity> (string)
 2525: 
 2526: One of C<'HIGH'>, C<'MEDIUM'>, C<'LOW'>, or C<'INFO'>.
 2527: 
 2528: =item C<flag> (string)
 2529: 
 2530: A lower-cased, underscore-separated machine-readable identifier.  See the
 2531: Algorithm section for the full list of possible flag names.
 2532: 
 2533: =item C<detail> (string)
 2534: 
 2535: A human-readable sentence describing the specific finding, including the
 2536: values from the message that triggered the flag (domain name, IP address,
 2537: header value, etc.).  Suitable for inclusion in an abuse report or log.
 2538: 
 2539: =back
 2540: 
 2541: The arrayref is empty (C<[]>) when no flags are raised.
 2542: 
 2543: =back
 2544: 
 2545: =head3 Side Effects
 2546: 
 2547: The first call triggers C<originating_ip()>, C<embedded_urls()>, and
 2548: C<mailto_domains()> if they have not already run on the current message.
 2549: Each of those methods may perform network I/O as documented in their own
 2550: entries.  Specifically:
 2551: 
 2552: =over 4
 2553: 
 2554: =item * C<originating_ip()> performs a PTR lookup and RDAP/WHOIS for the
 2555: sending IP.
 2556: 
 2557: =item * C<embedded_urls()> performs an A lookup and RDAP/WHOIS for each
 2558: unique URL hostname.
 2559: 
 2560: =item * C<mailto_domains()> performs A, MX, NS, and WHOIS queries for
 2561: each unique contact domain.
 2562: 
 2563: =back
 2564: 
 2565: All results are cached.  Subsequent calls to C<risk_assessment()> on the
 2566: same object return the cached hashref immediately.  The cache is invalidated
 2567: by C<parse_email()>.
 2568: 
 2569: =head3 Algorithm: flags and scoring
 2570: 
 2571: The following flags may be raised.  They are evaluated in five groups, in
 2572: the order shown.  The same flag name is never raised more than once per
 2573: message.
 2574: 
 2575: B<Group 1 -- Originating IP> (requires C<originating_ip()> to return a
 2576: result):
 2577: 
 2578: =over 4
 2579: 
 2580: =item C<residential_sending_ip> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2581: 
 2582: The rDNS of the sending IP matches patterns associated with residential
 2583: broadband or dynamically-assigned addresses: an embedded dotted-quad, or
 2584: any of the substrings C<dsl>, C<adsl>, C<cable>, C<broad>, C<dial>,
 2585: C<dynamic>, C<dhcp>, C<ppp>, C<residential>, C<cust>, C<home>, C<pool>,
 2586: C<client>, C<user>, C<staticN>, or C<hostN>.
 2587: 
 2588: =item C<no_reverse_dns> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2589: 
 2590: The sending IP has no PTR record, or the PTR lookup returned the sentinel
 2591: C<'(no reverse DNS)'>.  Legitimate mail servers invariably have rDNS.
 2592: 
 2593: =item C<low_confidence_origin> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2594: 
 2595: The originating IP was taken from an unverified header (C<X-Originating-IP>)
 2596: rather than from the C<Received:> chain.  Confidence level is C<'low'>.
 2597: 
 2598: =item C<high_spam_country> (INFO, weight 0)
 2599: 
 2600: The sending IP's country code is one of: C<CN> (China), C<RU> (Russia),
 2601: C<NG> (Nigeria), C<VN> (Vietnam), C<IN> (India), C<PK> (Pakistan),
 2602: C<BD> (Bangladesh).  Informational only; does not contribute to the score.
 2603: 
 2604: =back
 2605: 
 2606: B<Group 2 -- Email authentication> (from C<Authentication-Results:> header):
 2607: 
 2608: =over 4
 2609: 
 2610: =item C<spf_fail> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2611: 
 2612: SPF result is C<fail>, C<permerror>, C<temperror>, C<none>, or any value
 2613: other than C<pass> or C<softfail>.  The sending IP is not authorised by
 2614: the domain's SPF record.
 2615: 
 2616: =item C<spf_softfail> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2617: 
 2618: SPF result is C<softfail> (C<~all>).  The sending IP is not explicitly
 2619: authorised but the domain policy does not hard-fail it.
 2620: 
 2621: =item C<dkim_fail> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2622: 
 2623: DKIM result is present and is any value other than C<pass>.
 2624: 
 2625: =item C<dmarc_fail> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2626: 
 2627: DMARC result is present and is any value other than C<pass>.
 2628: 
 2629: =item C<dkim_domain_mismatch> (INFO or MEDIUM, weight 0 or 2)
 2630: 
 2631: The DKIM signing domain (C<d=> tag) differs from the registrable domain
 2632: of the C<From:> address.  Raised at INFO (weight 0) when DKIM passes --
 2633: this is normal for bulk senders using ESPs such as SendGrid or Mailchimp.
 2634: Raised at MEDIUM (weight 2) when DKIM fails or is absent -- a differing
 2635: domain combined with a failed signature is more suspicious.
 2636: 
 2637: =back
 2638: 
 2639: B<Group 3 -- Date: header>:
 2640: 
 2641: =over 4
 2642: 
 2643: =item C<missing_date> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2644: 
 2645: No C<Date:> header is present, or it contains only whitespace.  Violates
 2646: RFC 5322; common in programmatically-generated spam.
 2647: 
 2648: =item C<suspicious_date> (LOW, weight 1)
 2649: 
 2650: The C<Date:> header is present but more than 7 days in the past or more
 2651: than 7 days in the future relative to the time of analysis.  Timezone
 2652: offsets are ignored during comparison (maximum error: approximately 14
 2653: hours, well within the 7-day window).
 2654: 
 2655: =back
 2656: 
 2657: B<Group 4 -- Header identity and consistency>:
 2658: 
 2659: =over 4
 2660: 
 2661: =item C<display_name_domain_spoof> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2662: 
 2663: The C<From:> display name contains a domain name (matched against the
 2664: suffixes C<.com>, C<.net>, C<.org>, C<.io>, C<.co>, C<.uk>, C<.au>,
 2665: C<.gov>, C<.edu>) that differs at the registrable level from the actual
 2666: C<From:> address domain.  Example: C<"PayPal paypal.com" E<lt>phish@evil.exampleE<gt>>.
 2667: 
 2668: =item C<free_webmail_sender> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2669: 
 2670: The C<From:> address belongs to a free webmail provider: Gmail, Yahoo,
 2671: Hotmail, Outlook, Live, AOL, ProtonMail, Yandex, or mail.ru.
 2672: 
 2673: =item C<reply_to_differs_from_from> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2674: 
 2675: A C<Reply-To:> header is present and its email address differs from the
 2676: C<From:> address (case-insensitive comparison).  Replies will be harvested
 2677: by a different address than the apparent sender.
 2678: 
 2679: =item C<undisclosed_recipients> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2680: 
 2681: The C<To:> header is absent, empty, contains the string C<undisclosed>, or
 2682: matches the group-syntax sentinel C<:;>.
 2683: 
 2684: =item C<encoded_subject> (LOW, weight 1)
 2685: 
 2686: The C<Subject:> header contains a MIME encoded-word sequence
 2687: (C<=?charset?encoding?text?=>).  Often used to evade keyword filters.
 2688: 
 2689: =back
 2690: 
 2691: B<Group 5 -- URLs and domains> (from C<embedded_urls()> and
 2692: C<mailto_domains()>):
 2693: 
 2694: =over 4
 2695: 
 2696: =item C<url_shortener> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2697: 
 2698: At least one URL hostname is in the built-in URL shortener list (over 25
 2699: services including C<bit.ly>, C<tinyurl.com>, C<t.co>, C<ow.ly>, etc.).
 2700: Raised at most once per unique shortener hostname per message.
 2701: 
 2702: =item C<http_not_https> (LOW, weight 1)
 2703: 
 2704: At least one URL uses the plain C<http://> scheme rather than C<https://>.
 2705: Raised at most once per unique hostname.
 2706: 
 2707: =item C<recently_registered_domain> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2708: 
 2709: At least one contact domain was registered less than 180 days before the
 2710: time of analysis.
 2711: 
 2712: =item C<domain_expires_soon> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2713: 
 2714: At least one contact domain expires within the next 30 days.  Suggests a
 2715: throwaway domain.
 2716: 
 2717: =item C<domain_expired> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2718: 
 2719: At least one contact domain has already passed its expiry date.
 2720: 
 2721: =item C<lookalike_domain> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2722: 
 2723: At least one contact domain contains the name of a well-known brand
 2724: (C<paypal>, C<apple>, C<google>, C<amazon>, C<microsoft>, C<netflix>,
 2725: C<ebay>, C<instagram>, C<facebook>, C<twitter>, C<linkedin>,
 2726: C<bankofamerica>, C<wellsfargo>, C<chase>, C<barclays>, C<hsbc>,
 2727: C<lloyds>, C<santander>) but is not the brand's own canonical domain
 2728: (e.g. C<paypal.com>, C<paypal.co.uk>).
 2729: 
 2730: =back
 2731: 
 2732: =head3 Notes
 2733: 
 2734: =over 4
 2735: 
 2736: =item *
 2737: 
 2738: The C<flags> arrayref is a reference to the module's internal list.
 2739: Callers must not modify it.  To iterate safely, use C<@{ $risk-E<gt>{flags} }>.
 2740: 
 2741: =item *
 2742: 
 2743: Flags are not deduplicated across categories.  If C<spf_fail> and
 2744: C<dkim_fail> both apply, both appear in the list and both contribute to
 2745: the score.
 2746: 
 2747: =item *
 2748: 
 2749: C<high_spam_country> and C<dkim_domain_mismatch> (when DKIM passes)
 2750: contribute zero to the score.  Their presence does not change the level
 2751: classification, but they appear in the C<flags> list so callers can
 2752: include them in reports.
 2753: 
 2754: =item *
 2755: 
 2756: The level thresholds are fixed constants: HIGH >= 9, MEDIUM >= 5, LOW >= 2,
 2757: INFO < 2.  They are not configurable.
 2758: 
 2759: =item *
 2760: 
 2761: C<risk_assessment()> does not directly raise flags for domains found only
 2762: in URLs (C<embedded_urls()> hosts); domain checks in Group 5 apply only
 2763: to domains from C<mailto_domains()>.  URL hostname checks (shorteners,
 2764: HTTP) use the C<embedded_urls()> list.
 2765: 
 2766: =item *
 2767: 
 2768: If C<parse_email()> has not been called, or was called with an empty or
 2769: malformed message, C<risk_assessment()> returns a valid hashref with
 2770: C<level =E<gt> 'INFO'>, C<score =E<gt> 0>, and C<flags =E<gt> []>.
 2771: 
 2772: =back
 2773: 
 2774: =head3 API Specification
 2775: 
 2776: =head4 Input
 2777:

 3071: 
 3072: =head2 abuse_report_text()
 3073: 
 3074: Produces a compact, plain-text string intended to be sent as the body of
 3075: an abuse report email to an ISP or hosting provider.  It summarises the
 3076: risk level, lists every red flag with its detail, identifies the originating
 3077: IP and its network owner, lists the abuse contacts, and appends the complete
 3078: message headers so the recipient can trace the session in their own logs.
 3079: 
 3080: The message body is intentionally omitted to keep the report concise.
 3081: Headers are sufficient for an ISP to locate the relevant mail session; the
 3082: body adds bulk without aiding the investigation.
 3083: 
 3084: This method is the companion to C<abuse_contacts()>: call
 3085: C<abuse_contacts()> to obtain the addresses to send the report to, and
 3086: C<abuse_report_text()> to obtain the text to send.  Use C<report()> instead
 3087: when you want a comprehensive analyst-facing document rather than a
 3088: send-ready ISP report.
 3089: 
 3090: =head3 Usage
 3091: 
 3092:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 3093: 
 3094:     my $text     = $analyser->abuse_report_text();
 3095:     my @contacts = $analyser->abuse_contacts();
 3096: 
 3097:     for my $c (@contacts) {
 3098:         send_email(
 3099:             to      => $c->{address},
 3100:             subject => 'Abuse report: ' . ($analyser->originating_ip()->{ip} // 'unknown'),
 3101:             body    => $text,
 3102:         );
 3103:     }
 3104: 
 3105:     # Print to stdout for manual review before sending
 3106:     print $text;
 3107: 
 3108:     # Write to file for a ticketing system
 3109:     open my $fh, '>', 'abuse_report.txt' or die $!;
 3110:     print $fh $text;
 3111:     close $fh;
 3112: 
 3113: =head3 Arguments
 3114: 
 3115: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 3116: 
 3117: =head3 Returns
 3118: 
 3119: A plain scalar string containing the report text.  The string is
 3120: newline-terminated and uses Unix line endings (C<\n>) throughout.
 3121: The string is never empty; it always contains at least the boilerplate
 3122: introduction and the risk-level line, even if no red flags were found.
 3123: 
 3124: The report is structured as follows, in order:
 3125: 
 3126: =over 4
 3127: 
 3128: =item 1. Introduction
 3129: 
 3130: Two fixed lines:
 3131: 
 3132:     This is an automated abuse report generated by Email::Abuse::Investigator.
 3133:     Please investigate the following spam/phishing message.
 3134: 
 3135: =item 2. Risk level
 3136: 
 3137:     RISK LEVEL: HIGH (score: 11)
 3138: 
 3139: =item 3. Red flags (omitted if no flags were raised)
 3140: 
 3141:     RED FLAGS IDENTIFIED:
 3142:       [HIGH] firmluminary.com was registered 2025-09-01 (less than 180 days ago)
 3143:       [MEDIUM] rDNS 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au looks like a broadband line
 3144:       ...
 3145: 
 3146: Each flag is formatted as C<[SEVERITY] detail-string>, one per line,
 3147: indented two spaces.  The flag machine-name is not included; only the
 3148: human-readable detail string is shown, matching what a postmaster would
 3149: want to read.
 3150: 
 3151: =item 4. Originating IP (omitted if C<originating_ip()> returns C<undef>)
 3152: 
 3153:     ORIGINATING IP: 120.88.161.249 (120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au)
 3154:     NETWORK OWNER:  TPG Telecom Limited
 3155: 
 3156: =item 5. Abuse contacts (omitted if C<abuse_contacts()> returns an empty list)
 3157: 
 3158:     ABUSE CONTACTS:
 3159:       abuse@tpg.com.au (Sending ISP)
 3160:       abuse@registrar.example (Domain registrar for firmluminary.com)
 3161: 
 3162: =item 6. Original message headers
 3163: 
 3164:     ------------------------------------------------------------------------
 3165:     ORIGINAL MESSAGE HEADERS:
 3166:     ------------------------------------------------------------------------
 3167:     received: from 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au ...
 3168:     from: Sender <spammer@firmluminary.com>
 3169:     ...
 3170: 
 3171: All parsed headers are emitted, one per line, in the order they appeared
 3172: in the original message.  Header names are lower-cased (as normalised
 3173: during C<parse_email()>).  Header values are verbatim.  The message
 3174: body is not included.
 3175: 
 3176: =back
 3177: 
 3178: =head3 Side Effects
 3179: 
 3180: Calls C<risk_assessment()>, C<originating_ip()>, and C<abuse_contacts()>
 3181: if they have not already run, which in turn may perform network I/O as
 3182: documented in those methods.  All results are cached; the text is not
 3183: itself cached, but re-computing it is cheap since all the underlying data
 3184: is already cached.
 3185: 
 3186: =head3 Notes
 3187: 
 3188: =over 4
 3189: 
 3190: =item *
 3191: 
 3192: Header names in the output are lower-cased (e.g. C<from:>, C<received:>),
 3193: because that is how they are stored internally after C<parse_email()>
 3194: normalises them.  Postmasters are accustomed to receiving headers in their
 3195: original mixed case; if canonical capitalisation is required, a simple
 3196: substitution (C<s/^([\w-]+)/\u\L$1/>) will restore it.
 3197: 
 3198: =item *
 3199: 
 3200: The message body is deliberately excluded.  This avoids transmitting
 3201: potentially malicious or offensive content to third parties, keeps the
 3202: report below common size limits for abuse mailboxes, and is consistent
 3203: with the RFC 2646 / ARF (Abuse Reporting Format) practice of including
 3204: only the headers in a first-contact report.  To include the body, callers
 3205: can append C<$self-E<gt>{_raw}> directly, though this is not recommended.
 3206: 
 3207: =item *
 3208: 
 3209: The separator lines are exactly 72 hyphens (C<-> x 72), matching the
 3210: separator width used by C<report()>.
 3211: 
 3212: =item *
 3213: 
 3214: The output is suitable for use as a plain-text email body.  It is not
 3215: ARF (RFC 5965) compliant; it does not include a C<message/feedback-report>
 3216: MIME part.  For ARF-compliant reporting, use the output of this method as
 3217: the human-readable first part and add the ARF metadata separately.
 3218: 
 3219: =item *
 3220: 
 3221: If C<parse_email()> has not been called, all sections that depend on
 3222: analysis will be empty (no flags, no originating IP, no contacts) and the
 3223: header section will be blank.  The method will not die.
 3224: 
 3225: =back
 3226: 
 3227: =head3 API Specification
 3228: 
 3229: =head4 Input
 3230: 
 3231:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 3232:     # No arguments.
 3233:     []
 3234: 
 3235: =head4 Output
 3236: 
 3237:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 3238:     {
 3239:         type  => SCALAR,
 3240:         # Non-empty plain-text string, newline-terminated.
 3241:         # Always defined; never undef.
 3242:         # Line endings: Unix LF (\n) only.
 3243:         # Minimum content: introduction + risk-level line.
 3244:     }
 3245: 
 3246: =cut
 3247:

 3308: 
 3309: =head2 abuse_contacts()
 3310: 
 3311: Collates the complete set of parties that should receive an abuse report
 3312: for this message: the ISP that owns the sending IP, the operators of every
 3313: URL host, the web, mail, and DNS hosts of every contact domain, each
 3314: domain's registrar, the webmail or ESP account provider identified from
 3315: key headers, the DKIM signing organisation, and the ESP identified via
 3316: the C<List-Unsubscribe:> header.
 3317: 
 3318: For each party the method produces the role description, the abuse email
 3319: address, a supporting note, and the source of the information.  Addresses
 3320: are deduplicated globally: if the same address is discovered through
 3321: multiple routes (e.g. Google as both the sending ISP and the owner of a
 3322: blogspot.com URL in the message body), it appears only once.  The C<role>
 3323: string for that entry is the combined description of all routes that found
 3324: it, joined by C<" and ">, and the C<roles> key holds the individual role
 3325: strings as an arrayref.
 3326: 
 3327: This method is designed to be used together with C<abuse_report_text()>:
 3328: iterate over the returned contacts to obtain the list of addresses, and
 3329: send the text from C<abuse_report_text()> to each one.
 3330: 
 3331: =head3 Usage
 3332: 
 3333:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 3334:     my @contacts = $analyser->abuse_contacts();
 3335: 
 3336:     for my $c (@contacts) {
 3337:         printf "Role    : %s\n", $c->{role};
 3338:         printf "Send to : %s\n", $c->{address};
 3339:         printf "Note    : %s\n", $c->{note}  if $c->{note};
 3340:         printf "Source  : %s\n", $c->{via};
 3341:         print  "\n";
 3342:     }
 3343: 
 3344:     # Collect addresses for sending
 3345:     my @addresses = map { $_->{address} } @contacts;
 3346: 
 3347:     # Filter to WHOIS-discovered contacts only
 3348:     my @whois_contacts = grep { $_->{via} =~ /whois/ } @contacts;
 3349: 
 3350:     # Check whether any registrar abuse contacts were found
 3351:     my @registrar = grep { $_->{role} =~ /registrar/ } @contacts;
 3352: 
 3353: =head3 Arguments
 3354: 
 3355: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 3356: 
 3357: =head3 Returns
 3358: 
 3359: A list (not an arrayref) of hashrefs, one per unique abuse contact address,
 3360: in the order they were first discovered.  Returns an empty list if no
 3361: actionable abuse contacts can be determined, or if C<parse_email()> has
 3362: not been called.
 3363: 
 3364: Returns a de-duplicated list of hashrefs, one per party that should
 3365: receive an abuse report, in priority order:
 3366: 
 3367:     {
 3368:         role    => 'Sending ISP',          # human-readable role
 3369:         address => 'abuse@senderisp.example',
 3370:         note    => 'IP block 120.88.0.0/14 owner',
 3371:         via     => 'ip-whois',             # ip-whois | domain-whois | provider-table | rdap
 3372:     }
 3373: 
 3374: Roles produced (in order):
 3375: 
 3376:   Sending ISP            - network owner of the originating IP
 3377:   URL host               - network owner of each unique web-server IP
 3378:   Mail host (MX)         - network owner of the domain's MX record IP
 3379:   DNS host (NS)          - network owner of the authoritative NS IP
 3380:   Domain registrar       - registrar abuse contact from domain WHOIS
 3381:   Account provider       - e.g. Gmail / Outlook for the From:/Sender: account
 3382:   DKIM signer            - the organisation whose key signed the message
 3383:   ESP / bulk sender      - identified via List-Unsubscribe: domain
 3384: 
 3385: Addresses are deduplicated so the same address never appears twice,
 3386: even if it is discovered through multiple routes.
 3387: 
 3388: Each hashref contains the following keys, all always present:
 3389: 
 3390: =over 4
 3391: 
 3392: =item C<role> (string)
 3393: 
 3394: A human-readable description of the party's relationship to the message.
 3395: When the same address was found via multiple discovery routes, the role
 3396: strings from each route are joined with C<" and "> (e.g.
 3397: C<"Sending ISP (provider table) and URL host (provider table)">).
 3398: See the Algorithm section for the full set of role string patterns.
 3399: 
 3400: =item C<roles> (arrayref of strings)
 3401: 
 3402: The individual role strings for each discovery route that found this
 3403: address, in discovery order.  Contains exactly one element when the
 3404: address was found via a single route; two or more elements when multiple
 3405: routes converged on the same address.  The C<role> key is always the
 3406: C<join(' and ', @{$c->{roles}})> of this arrayref.
 3407: 
 3408: =item C<address> (string)
 3409: 
 3410: The abuse contact email address, lower-cased.  Always contains an C<@>
 3411: sign.  Deduplicated globally: each distinct address appears at most once
 3412: across the entire list, regardless of how many discovery routes found it.
 3413: 
 3414: =item C<note> (string)
 3415: 
 3416: Supporting information about why this party was identified and what action
 3417: to request.  For provider-table entries this is the note from the built-in
 3418: table (which may include a URL to a web-based abuse form).  For WHOIS- and
 3419: RDAP-discovered entries this describes the IP block or domain involved.
 3420: Always defined; may be the empty string for entries where no note is
 3421: available.  When roles are merged, this reflects the note from the first
 3422: discovery route.
 3423: 
 3424: =item C<via> (string)
 3425: 
 3426: The discovery method for the first route that found this address.  One of:
 3427: 
 3428: =over 8
 3429: 
 3430: =item C<'provider-table'>
 3431: 
 3432: The address was found in the module's built-in table of well-known
 3433: providers (Google, Microsoft, Cloudflare, SendGrid, Mailchimp, etc.).
 3434: Provider-table addresses take priority over WHOIS for the same entity
 3435: because they are curated and point to the right team, whereas generic
 3436: WHOIS contacts sometimes route to NOCs rather than abuse desks.
 3437: 
 3438: =item C<'ip-whois'>
 3439: 
 3440: The address was obtained from an RDAP or WHOIS lookup on an IP block
 3441: (the sending IP, a URL host IP, or an MX/NS IP).
 3442: 
 3443: =item C<'domain-whois'>
 3444: 
 3445: The address was obtained from a WHOIS lookup on a domain name (registrar
 3446: abuse contact from the C<Registrar Abuse Contact Email:> or equivalent
 3447: field).
 3448: 
 3449: =back
 3450: 
 3451: =back
 3452: 
 3453: =head3 Side Effects
 3454: 
 3455: Triggers C<originating_ip()>, C<embedded_urls()>, and C<mailto_domains()>
 3456: if they have not already run on the current message, performing all
 3457: associated network I/O as documented in those methods.  Additionally
 3458: consults the built-in provider table and the cached authentication results;
 3459: neither requires network I/O.
 3460: 
 3461: The result is not independently cached.  Each call recomputes the contact
 3462: list from the cached results of the underlying methods.  Because those
 3463: results are cached, subsequent calls are fast (no network I/O), but they
 3464: do re-execute the collation and deduplication logic.
 3465: 
 3466: =head3 Algorithm: discovery routes
 3467: 
 3468: Contacts are discovered through six routes, applied in order.
 3469: Deduplication is global across all routes: if an address is found by
 3470: more than one route, a single entry is kept and the role strings from
 3471: every route that found it are accumulated into C<roles> and joined into
 3472: C<role>.  An entry is suppressed entirely if its address is empty, does
 3473: not contain an C<@> sign, or is the sentinel C<'(unknown)'>.
 3474: 
 3475: =over 4
 3476: 
 3477: =item Route 1 -- Sending ISP
 3478: 
 3479: The originating IP from C<originating_ip()> is looked up in the built-in
 3480: provider table (by rDNS hostname, stripping subdomains until a match is
 3481: found).  If found, a C<provider-table> entry is added with role
 3482: C<"Sending ISP (provider table)">.
 3483: 
 3484: The C<abuse> field from C<originating_ip()> (obtained from RDAP/WHOIS) is
 3485: then added as an C<ip-whois> entry with role C<"Sending ISP">, unless it
 3486: is C<'(unknown)'>.
 3487: 
 3488: =item Route 2 -- URL hosts
 3489: 
 3490: For each unique hostname in C<embedded_urls()>, the built-in provider
 3491: table is consulted (by hostname, stripping subdomains).  If found, a
 3492: C<provider-table> entry is added with role C<"URL host (provider table)">.
 3493: 
 3494: The C<abuse> field from the URL hashref is then added as an C<ip-whois>
 3495: entry with role C<"URL host">, unless it is C<'(unknown)'>.
 3496: 
 3497: Each unique hostname is processed at most once; multiple URLs on the same
 3498: host do not generate multiple contacts.
 3499: 
 3500: =item Route 3 -- Contact domain hosting and registration
 3501: 
 3502: For each domain from C<mailto_domains()>, up to four contacts may be
 3503: generated:
 3504: 
 3505: =over 8
 3506: 
 3507: =item *
 3508: 
 3509: B<Web host>: if C<web_abuse> is present, both a provider-table lookup
 3510: on the domain name and the WHOIS-derived C<web_abuse> address are tried.
 3511: Role: C<"Web host of $domain"> or C<"Web host of $domain (provider table)">.
 3512: 
 3513: =item *
 3514: 
 3515: B<Mail host (MX)>: if C<mx_abuse> is present.
 3516: Role: C<"Mail host (MX) for $domain">, via C<ip-whois>.
 3517: 
 3518: =item *
 3519: 
 3520: B<DNS host (NS)>: if C<ns_abuse> is present.
 3521: Role: C<"DNS host (NS) for $domain">, via C<ip-whois>.
 3522: 
 3523: =item *
 3524: 
 3525: B<Domain registrar>: if C<registrar_abuse> is present.
 3526: Role: C<"Domain registrar for $domain">, via C<domain-whois>.
 3527: 
 3528: =back
 3529: 
 3530: =item Route 4 -- Account provider
 3531: 
 3532: The C<From:>, C<Reply-To:>, C<Return-Path:>, and C<Sender:> header values
 3533: are inspected in that order.  The domain portion of each address is looked
 3534: up in the built-in provider table (stripping subdomains until a match).
 3535: If found, a C<provider-table> entry is added with role
 3536: C<"Account provider ($header: $value)">.  This identifies the webmail
 3537: or ESP service that hosts the sender's account.
 3538: 
 3539: =item Route 5 -- DKIM signing organisation
 3540: 
 3541: The C<d=> tag from the C<DKIM-Signature:> header is looked up in the
 3542: built-in provider table.  If found, a C<provider-table> entry is added
 3543: with role C<"DKIM signer (provider table): $domain">.  The full domain
 3544: pipeline (web/MX/NS/WHOIS) for this domain is already handled via Route 3
 3545: through C<mailto_domains()>.
 3546: 
 3547: =item Route 6 -- ESP / bulk sender (List-Unsubscribe)
 3548: 
 3549: Both C<https://> URLs and C<mailto:> addresses in the C<List-Unsubscribe:>
 3550: header are parsed for their domains.  Each unique domain is looked up in
 3551: the built-in provider table.  If found, a C<provider-table> entry is added
 3552: with role C<"ESP / bulk sender (List-Unsubscribe: $domain)">.
 3553: 
 3554: =back
 3555: 
 3556: =head3 Notes
 3557: 
 3558: =over 4
 3559: 
 3560: =item *
 3561: 
 3562: Deduplication is by lower-cased address only.  Two contacts with different
 3563: roles but the same address result in a single entry using the data from
 3564: whichever route found it first.  The later route's role and note are
 3565: silently discarded.
 3566: 
 3567: =item *
 3568: 
 3569: The provider table contains curated entries for approximately 50
 3570: well-known domains including major webmail providers (Gmail, Outlook,
 3571: Yahoo, Apple), CDNs and hosters (Cloudflare, Fastly, Akamai, AWS,
 3572: DigitalOcean, Vultr, Hetzner, Contabo, Leaseweb, M247, OVH, Linode),
 3573: ESPs (SendGrid, Mailchimp, Mailgun, Postmark, Brevo, Klaviyo, Campaign
 3574: Monitor, Constant Contact, HubSpot), registrars (GoDaddy, Namecheap),
 3575: and ISPs (TPG, Internode).  Subdomain matching strips labels left-to-right
 3576: until a match is found, so C<mail.sendgrid.net> matches C<sendgrid.net>.
 3577: 
 3578: =item *
 3579: 
 3580: Provider-table entries take priority in the sense that they are added
 3581: first; if the WHOIS address happens to match the provider-table address,
 3582: the WHOIS entry is suppressed by deduplication.  If they differ (unusual
 3583: but possible), both are added.
 3584: 
 3585: =item *
 3586: 
 3587: The result is not cached.  If you call C<abuse_contacts()> multiple times
 3588: on the same object, the full collation runs each time.  If this is a
 3589: concern, store the result in a variable:
 3590: C<my @contacts = $analyser-E<gt>abuse_contacts()>.
 3591: 
 3592: =item *
 3593: 
 3594: An empty list is returned if the message has no usable originating IP, no
 3595: extractable URLs, no contact domains, and no recognised provider-table
 3596: matches.  This is unusual in practice but can occur for very sparse or
 3597: malformed messages.
 3598: 
 3599: =back
 3600: 
 3601: =head3 API Specification
 3602: 
 3603: =head4 Input
 3604: 
 3605:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 3606:     # No arguments.
 3607:     []
 3608: 
 3609: =head4 Output
 3610: 
 3611:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 3612: 
 3613:     # A list (possibly empty) of hashrefs, in discovery order:
 3614:     (
 3615:         {
 3616:             type => HASHREF,
 3617:             keys => {
 3618:                 role => {
 3619:                     type => SCALAR,
 3620:                     # Human-readable role description; always defined,
 3621:                     # may contain inline domain/IP/header values.
 3622:                 },
 3623:                 address => {
 3624:                     type  => SCALAR,
 3625:                     regex => qr/^[^\s@]+\@[^\s@]+$/,
 3626:                     # Lower-cased email address; unique across the list.
 3627:                 },
 3628:                 note => {
 3629:                     type => SCALAR,
 3630:                     # Supporting detail; always defined, may be empty string.
 3631:                 },
 3632:                 via => {
 3633:                     type  => SCALAR,
 3634:                     regex => qr/^(?:provider-table|ip-whois|domain-whois)$/,
 3635:                 },
 3636:             },
 3637:         },
 3638:         # ... one hashref per unique address, in first-discovered order
 3639:     )
 3640: 
 3641:     # Empty list when no actionable abuse contacts can be determined.
 3642: 
 3643: =cut
 3644:

 3923: 
 3924: =head2 form_contacts()
 3925: 
 3926: Returns the list of parties that require abuse reports to be submitted via
 3927: a web form rather than (or in addition to) email.  These are providers whose
 3928: C<%PROVIDER_ABUSE> entry has a C<form> key.  Each hashref contains the form
 3929: URL, instructions on what to paste, instructions on what to upload (if
 3930: applicable), the role, and the discovery note.
 3931: 
 3932: Returns a list (not an arrayref) of hashrefs, one per unique form contact,
 3933: in discovery order.  Returns an empty list if no form-only or form-plus-email
 3934: contacts are found.
 3935: 
 3936: Each hashref contains:
 3937: 
 3938: =over 4
 3939: 
 3940: =item C<form> (string) -- the URL of the web form
 3941: 
 3942: =item C<role> (string) -- human-readable role, same format as C<abuse_contacts()>
 3943: 
 3944: =item C<note> (string) -- supporting detail about the provider
 3945: 
 3946: =item C<form_paste> (string, optional) -- what text to paste into the form
 3947: 
 3948: =item C<form_upload> (string, optional) -- what file to attach to the form
 3949: 
 3950: =item C<via> (string) -- always C<'provider-table'>
 3951: 
 3952: =back
 3953: 
 3954: =cut

 4103: 
 4104: =head2 report()
 4105: 
 4106: Returns a formatted plain-text abuse report.
 4107: 
 4108: Produces a comprehensive, analyst-facing plain-text report covering all
 4109: findings from every analysis method.  It is the single-document summary
 4110: of everything the module knows about a message: envelope fields, risk
 4111: assessment, originating host, sending software, received chain tracking
 4112: IDs, embedded URLs grouped by hostname, contact domain intelligence, and
 4113: the recommended abuse contacts.
 4114: 
 4115: Use C<report()> when you want a human-readable document for review,
 4116: logging, or a ticketing system.  Use C<abuse_report_text()> when you want
 4117: a compact string to transmit to an ISP abuse desk.
 4118: 
 4119: =head3 Usage
 4120: 
 4121:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 4122:     my $text = $analyser->report();
 4123:     print $text;
 4124: 
 4125:     # Write to a file
 4126:     open my $fh, '>', 'report.txt' or die $!;
 4127:     print $fh $analyser->report();
 4128:     close $fh;
 4129: 
 4130:     # Log the risk level line from the report
 4131:     my ($level_line) = $analyser->report() =~ /(\[ RISK ASSESSMENT: [^\]]+\])/;
 4132:     $logger->info($level_line);
 4133: 
 4134:     # Check idempotency -- safe to call multiple times
 4135:     my $r1 = $analyser->report();
 4136:     my $r2 = $analyser->report();
 4137:     # $r1 eq $r2 is always true for the same parsed message
 4138: 
 4139: =head3 Arguments
 4140: 
 4141: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 4142: 
 4143: =head3 Returns
 4144: 
 4145: A plain scalar string containing the full report, newline-terminated,
 4146: using Unix line endings (C<\n>) throughout.  The string is never empty;
 4147: it always contains at least the header banner and envelope summary section.
 4148: 
 4149: The report is structured as nine sections separated by blank lines, in
 4150: this fixed order:
 4151: 
 4152: =over 4
 4153: 
 4154: =item 1. Banner
 4155: 
 4156:     ========================================================================
 4157:       Email::Abuse::Investigator Report  (vX.XX)
 4158:     ========================================================================
 4159: 
 4160: A row of 72 equals signs, the module name and version number, and a
 4161: closing row of 72 equals signs.
 4162: 
 4163: =item 2. Envelope summary
 4164: 
 4165: Up to six header fields, each decoded from MIME encoded-words where
 4166: applicable.  If a field was encoded, the decoded form is shown first
 4167: followed by the raw encoded original in brackets:
 4168: 
 4169:     From           : PayPal Security <phish@evil.example>
 4170:     Reply-to       : Replies <harvest@collector.example>
 4171:     Return-path    : <phish@evil.example>
 4172:     Subject        : Account Alert  [encoded: =?UTF-8?B?QWNjb3VudA==?=]
 4173:     Date           : Mon, 01 Jan 2024 00:00:00 +0000
 4174:     Message-id     : <msg001@evil.example>
 4175: 
 4176: Fields examined (in order): C<From:>, C<Reply-To:>, C<Return-Path:>,
 4177: C<Subject:>, C<Date:>, C<Message-ID:>.  Fields not present in the message
 4178: are silently omitted.
 4179: 
 4180: =item 3. Risk assessment
 4181: 
 4182:     [ RISK ASSESSMENT: HIGH (score: 11) ]
 4183:       [HIGH] firmluminary.com was registered 2025-09-01 (less than 180 days ago)
 4184:       [MEDIUM] rDNS 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au looks like a broadband/residential line
 4185:       ...
 4186: 
 4187: Or, when no flags were raised:
 4188: 
 4189:     [ RISK ASSESSMENT: INFO (score: 0) ]
 4190:       (no specific red flags detected)
 4191: 
 4192: Each flag is shown as C<[SEVERITY] detail-string>.
 4193: 
 4194: =item 4. Originating host
 4195: 
 4196:     [ ORIGINATING HOST ]
 4197:       IP           : 120.88.161.249
 4198:       Reverse DNS  : 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au
 4199:       Country      : AU
 4200:       Organisation : TPG Telecom Limited
 4201:       Abuse addr   : abuse@tpg.com.au
 4202:       Confidence   : high
 4203:       Note         : First external hop in Received: chain
 4204: 
 4205: Or C<(could not determine originating IP)> if C<originating_ip()> returns
 4206: C<undef>.  Fields with no value are omitted.
 4207: 
 4208: =item 5. Sending software (omitted entirely if no software headers found)
 4209: 
 4210:     [ SENDING SOFTWARE / INFRASTRUCTURE CLUES ]
 4211:       x-php-originating-script : 1000:mailer.php
 4212:       Note           : PHP script on shared hosting -- report to hosting abuse team
 4213: 
 4214: One block per detected header, with its note.
 4215: 
 4216: =item 6. Received chain tracking IDs (omitted if no hops have id or for fields)
 4217: 
 4218:     [ RECEIVED CHAIN TRACKING IDs ]
 4219:       (Supply these to the relevant ISP abuse team to trace the session)
 4220: 
 4221:       IP           : 91.198.174.5
 4222:       Envelope for : victim@bandsman.co.uk
 4223:       Server ID    : ABC123XYZ
 4224: 
 4225: Only hops that have at least one of a session ID (C<id>) or envelope
 4226: recipient (C<for>) are shown; IP-only hops are suppressed.  Oldest hop
 4227: first.
 4228: 
 4229: =item 7. Embedded HTTP/HTTPS URLs
 4230: 
 4231:     [ EMBEDDED HTTP/HTTPS URLs ]
 4232:       Host         : bit.ly  *** URL SHORTENER - real destination hidden ***
 4233:       IP           : 67.199.248.11
 4234:       Country      : US
 4235:       Organisation : Bit.ly LLC
 4236:       Abuse addr   : abuse@bit.ly
 4237:       URL          : https://bit.ly/scam123
 4238: 
 4239: URLs are grouped by hostname; if multiple URLs share a hostname, all
 4240: paths are listed together under the single host block.  Known URL
 4241: shorteners are annotated inline.  Shown as C<(none found)> when the
 4242: body contains no HTTP/HTTPS URLs.
 4243: 
 4244: =item 8. Contact / reply-to domains
 4245: 
 4246:     [ CONTACT / REPLY-TO DOMAINS ]
 4247:       Domain       : firmluminary.com
 4248:       Found in     : From: header
 4249:       *** WARNING: RECENTLY REGISTERED - possible phishing domain ***
 4250:       Registered   : 2025-09-01
 4251:       Expires      : 2026-09-01
 4252:       Registrar    : GoDaddy.com LLC
 4253:       Reg. abuse   : abuse@godaddy.com
 4254:       Web host IP  : 104.21.30.10
 4255:       Web host org : Cloudflare Inc
 4256:       Web abuse    : abuse@cloudflare.com
 4257:       MX host      : mail.firmluminary.com
 4258:       MX IP        : 198.51.100.5
 4259:       MX org       : Hosting Corp
 4260:       MX abuse     : abuse@hostingcorp.example
 4261:       NS host      : ns1.cloudflare.com
 4262:       NS IP        : 173.245.58.51
 4263:       NS org       : Cloudflare Inc
 4264:       NS abuse     : abuse@cloudflare.com
 4265: 
 4266: One block per domain from C<mailto_domains()>.  Recently-registered
 4267: domains receive an inline warning banner.  Shown as C<(none found)>
 4268: when no qualifying contact domains are present.
 4269: 
 4270: =item 9. Where to send abuse reports
 4271: 
 4272:     [ WHERE TO SEND ABUSE REPORTS ]
 4273:       Role         : Sending ISP
 4274:       Send to      : abuse@tpg.com.au
 4275:       Note         : Network owner of originating IP 120.88.161.249 (TPG Telecom)
 4276:       Discovered   : ip-whois
 4277: 
 4278:       Role         : Domain registrar for firmluminary.com
 4279:       Send to      : abuse@godaddy.com
 4280:       Note         : Registrar: GoDaddy.com LLC
 4281:       Discovered   : domain-whois
 4282: 
 4283: One block per contact from C<abuse_contacts()>.  Shown as
 4284: C<(no abuse contacts could be determined)> when the list is empty.
 4285: 
 4286: =back
 4287: 
 4288: The report ends with a closing row of 72 equals signs.
 4289: 
 4290: =head3 Side Effects
 4291: 
 4292: Calls C<risk_assessment()>, C<originating_ip()>, C<sending_software()>,
 4293: C<received_trail()>, C<embedded_urls()>, C<mailto_domains()>, and
 4294: C<abuse_contacts()> if they have not already run on the current message,
 4295: performing all associated network I/O as documented in those methods.  All
 4296: underlying results are cached; the report text itself is not cached, but
 4297: re-computation is inexpensive since the data is already available.
 4298: 
 4299: =head3 Notes
 4300: 
 4301: =over 4
 4302: 
 4303: =item *
 4304: 
 4305: The report is idempotent: calling C<report()> multiple times on the same
 4306: object always returns an identical string, because all underlying methods
 4307: are cached.
 4308: 
 4309: =item *
 4310: 
 4311: MIME encoded-words in the C<From:>, C<Subject:>, and other displayed
 4312: headers are decoded for readability.  When a header was encoded, both the
 4313: decoded form and the raw encoded original are shown, so the report is
 4314: useful both for human reading and for log parsing.
 4315: 
 4316: =item *
 4317: 
 4318: URL hosts in section 7 are grouped by hostname and shown in first-seen
 4319: order.  Multiple URLs on the same host are listed together rather than
 4320: repeating the host's IP and WHOIS information, keeping the output compact
 4321: even when a message contains dozens of tracking-pixel and click-redirect
 4322: URLs all on the same CDN.
 4323: 
 4324: =item *
 4325: 
 4326: The received-trail section (section 6) filters out hops that have only an
 4327: IP address and no C<id> or C<for> clause.  The full unfiltered trail is
 4328: available via C<received_trail()>.
 4329: 
 4330: =item *
 4331: 
 4332: Section 5 (sending software) and section 6 (received chain tracking IDs)
 4333: are entirely omitted -- no heading, no placeholder text -- when no relevant
 4334: headers are present.  All other sections always appear, using a
 4335: C<(none found)> or equivalent placeholder when their data is empty.
 4336: 
 4337: =item *
 4338: 
 4339: The version number in the banner is the value of C<$Email::Abuse::Investigator::VERSION>
 4340: at the time C<report()> is called.
 4341: 
 4342: =back
 4343: 
 4344: =head3 API Specification
 4345: 
 4346: =head4 Input
 4347: 
 4348:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 4349:     # No arguments.
 4350:     []
 4351: 
 4352: =head4 Output
 4353: 
 4354:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 4355:     {
 4356:         type  => SCALAR,
 4357:         # Non-empty plain-text string, newline-terminated (\n).
 4358:         # Always defined; never undef.
 4359:         # Line endings: Unix LF (\n) only.
 4360:         # Structure: nine fixed sections in the order documented above,
 4361:         #            separated by blank lines, framed by 72-character
 4362:         #            equals-sign banners.
 4363:     }
 4364: 
 4365: =cut
 4366:

 4581: 
 4582: # _split_message( $text )
 4583: #
 4584: # Entry criteria:
 4585: #   $text  -- a defined scalar containing a raw RFC 2822 email message,
 4586: #             with headers and body separated by a blank line (\n\n or
 4587: #             \r\n\r\n).  Both LF and CRLF line endings are accepted.
 4588: #             The text must already be dereferenced (parse_email() handles
 4589: #             the scalar-ref case before calling this method).
 4590: #             Called only from parse_email(); $self->{_sending_sw} and
 4591: #             $self->{_rcvd_tracking} must have been reset to [] by the
 4592: #             caller before this method is invoked.
 4593: #
 4594: # Exit status:
 4595: #   Returns undef (and does nothing further) if $header_block is undef or
 4596: #   contains only whitespace -- i.e. the message has no headers or is
 4597: #   empty.  Otherwise returns no meaningful value; all results are
 4598: #   communicated through side effects on $self.
 4599: #
 4600: # Side effects:
 4601: #   $self->{_headers}      set to an arrayref of { name => lc, value => raw }
 4602: #                          hashrefs, one per parsed header, in message order.
 4603: #                          Folded (multi-line) values are unfolded before
 4604: #                          parsing (RFC 2822 s2.2.3).  Header names are
 4605: #                          normalised to lower-case.
 4606: #   $self->{_received}     set to an arrayref of raw Received: header values
 4607: #                          (not decoded), in message order (most-recent first).
 4608: #   $self->{_body_plain}   set to the decoded plain-text body.  Appended to
 4609: #                          (not replaced) for each text/* part in multipart
 4610: #                          messages.
 4611: #   $self->{_body_html}    set to the decoded HTML body.  Appended to for
 4612: #                          each text/html part in multipart messages.
 4613: #   $self->{_sending_sw}   populated with { header, value, note } hashrefs
 4614: #                          for any of the six recognised software-fingerprint
 4615: #                          headers that are present, in alphabetical key order.
 4616: #   $self->{_rcvd_tracking} populated with { received, ip, for, id } hashrefs,
 4617: #                          one per Received: hop from which at least one of
 4618: #                          an IP, envelope recipient, or session ID could be
 4619: #                          extracted, in oldest-first order.
 4620: #
 4621: # Notes:
 4622: #   Delegates body decoding to _decode_multipart() for multipart/* content
 4623: #   types (which recursively handles each part) or to _decode_body() for
 4624: #   single-part messages.  If Content-Type is absent or unrecognised, the
 4625: #   body is treated as plain text with 7bit encoding.
 4626: #   The boundary parameter in multipart Content-Type is extracted with a
 4627: #   simple regex; missing or malformed boundaries cause the body to be
 4628: #   silently skipped.
 4629: #   Lines that do not match the header pattern /^([\w-]+)\s*:\s*(.*)/ are
 4630: #   silently discarded (covers blank lines and non-header preamble text).
 4631: 
 4632: sub _split_message {

 4642: 
 4643:     my @headers;

 4645:         if ($line =~ /^([\w-]+)\s*:\s*(.*)/) {

 4767: 
 4768: # _find_origin()
 4769: #
 4770: #   Identifies the IP address of the machine that originally injected the
 4771: #   message into the public mail system by walking the Received: chain and
 4772: #   discarding every hop that belongs to private, reserved, or
 4773: #   caller-trusted infrastructure.  The first remaining (oldest external)
 4774: #   IP is enriched with reverse DNS, organisation, abuse contact, and
 4775: #   country information and returned as the origin hashref.
 4776: #
 4777: #   This is the back-end implementation for the public originating_ip()
 4778: #   method, which caches the result.  _find_origin() itself performs no
 4779: #   caching and must not be called directly; always call originating_ip().
 4780: #
 4781: # Entry criteria:
 4782: #   No arguments beyond $self.
 4783: #   $self->{_received}     must be populated (by _split_message()).
 4784: #   $self->{_headers}      must be populated (by _split_message()), so
 4785: #                          that _header_value('x-originating-ip') works.
 4786: #   $self->{trusted_relays} must be an arrayref (set by new(); may be []).
 4787: #
 4788: # Exit status:
 4789: #   Returns a hashref on success -- the same structure as originating_ip():
 4790: #     { ip, rdns, org, abuse, country, confidence, note }
 4791: #   Returns undef if no usable originating IP can be determined:
 4792: #     -- all Received: IPs are private, reserved, or trusted; AND
 4793: #     -- X-Originating-IP is absent, private, or unparseable.
 4794: #
 4795: # Side effects:
 4796: #   Performs network I/O via _enrich_ip():
 4797: #     - one PTR (rDNS) lookup for the chosen IP (_reverse_dns)
 4798: #     - one RDAP or WHOIS query for the chosen IP (_whois_ip)
 4799: #   No state is written to $self; the result is returned, not cached here.
 4800: #
 4801: # Notes:
 4802: #   The Received: chain is walked in reverse message order -- i.e. from
 4803: #   the oldest header (bottom of the header block) to the most recent --
 4804: #   so that candidates are accumulated in oldest-first order.  $candidates[0]
 4805: #   is always the outermost (first) external relay.
 4806: #
 4807: #   Confidence levels are assigned as follows:
 4808: #     'high'   -- two or more distinct external IPs found in the chain.
 4809: #                 Multiple independent relay records corroborate the origin.
 4810: #     'medium' -- exactly one external IP found in the chain.
 4811: #     'low'    -- no usable Received: IP; origin taken from
 4812: #                 X-Originating-IP, which is injected by webmail providers
 4813: #                 and is not independently verifiable.  Brackets and
 4814: #                 whitespace are stripped from the header value before use.
 4815: #
 4816: #   _is_private() treats undef and the empty string as private, so a
 4817: #   Received: header from which no IP can be extracted is silently skipped
 4818: #   without special-casing.
 4819: #
 4820: #   IPv6 addresses are not extracted by _extract_ip_from_received(); only
 4821: #   dotted-quad IPv4 addresses are considered.
 4822:

 5097: 
 5098: # Full domain intelligence gathering
 5099: #
 5100: # _analyse_domain( $domain )
 5101: #
 5102: #   Runs the complete intelligence pipeline for a single domain name:
 5103: #   resolves its web-hosting IP (A record), mail-hosting IP (MX record),
 5104: #   DNS-hosting IP (NS record), and queries WHOIS for registrar, creation
 5105: #   date, expiry date, and abuse contact.  Each IP is enriched with
 5106: #   organisation name and abuse address via RDAP or WHOIS.
 5107: #
 5108: #   The result is cached in $self->{_domain_info}{$domain} so that if
 5109: #   the same domain is encountered in multiple sources (e.g. From: header
 5110: #   and body) the network queries are only performed once.
 5111: #
 5112: #   Called exclusively from _extract_and_analyse_domains(), which merges
 5113: #   the returned hashref with the { domain, source } record to produce
 5114: #   the per-domain hashrefs returned by mailto_domains().
 5115: #
 5116: # Entry criteria:
 5117: #   $domain  -- a defined, non-empty, lower-cased domain string with no
 5118: #               trailing dot (normalisation is the caller's responsibility).
 5119: #               Must not be in %TRUSTED_DOMAINS (filtering is the caller's
 5120: #               responsibility).
 5121: #   $self->{timeout}  -- used for all DNS and WHOIS socket operations.
 5122: #   $self->{_domain_info}  -- hashref cache; may already contain an entry
 5123: #                             for $domain from a prior call.
 5124: #
 5125: # Exit status:
 5126: #   Always returns a hashref reference -- never undef, never dies.
 5127: #   The hashref may be empty ({}) if all lookups fail or return nothing.
 5128: #   Keys present depend entirely on what the lookups return; all are
 5129: #   optional.  Possible keys and their types:
 5130: #     web_ip              string  -- dotted-quad IPv4 of A record
 5131: #     web_org             string  -- organisation owning web_ip
 5132: #     web_abuse           string  -- abuse contact for web_ip network
 5133: #     mx_host             string  -- lowest-preference MX hostname
 5134: #     mx_ip               string  -- dotted-quad IPv4 of mx_host
 5135: #     mx_org              string  -- organisation owning mx_ip
 5136: #     mx_abuse            string  -- abuse contact for mx_ip network
 5137: #     ns_host             string  -- first NS hostname returned
 5138: #     ns_ip               string  -- dotted-quad IPv4 of ns_host
 5139: #     ns_org              string  -- organisation owning ns_ip
 5140: #     ns_abuse            string  -- abuse contact for ns_ip network
 5141: #     registrar           string  -- registrar name from WHOIS
 5142: #     registrar_abuse     string  -- registrar abuse email from WHOIS
 5143: #     registered          string  -- creation date YYYY-MM-DD
 5144: #     expires             string  -- expiry date YYYY-MM-DD
 5145: #     recently_registered integer -- 1 if registered < 180 days ago
 5146: #     whois_raw           string  -- first 2048 bytes of WHOIS response
 5147: #
 5148: # Side effects:
 5149: #   Network I/O, subject to $self->{timeout}, in this order:
 5150: #     1. One A record lookup (_resolve_host) for the domain itself.
 5151: #     2. If web_ip found: one RDAP/WHOIS query (_whois_ip) -- up to two
 5152: #        TCP connections (IANA referral + authoritative registry).
 5153: #     3. If Net::DNS available: one MX record lookup.
 5154: #        If MX found: one A lookup for the MX hostname, then one
 5155: #        RDAP/WHOIS query for its IP (up to two TCP connections).
 5156: #     4. If Net::DNS available: one NS record lookup.
 5157: #        If NS found: one A lookup for the NS hostname, then one
 5158: #        RDAP/WHOIS query for its IP (up to two TCP connections).
 5159: #     5. Two TCP WHOIS connections for the domain itself: first to
 5160: #        whois.iana.org to obtain the TLD's authoritative registry,
 5161: #        then to that registry.
 5162: #   Worst-case total: 3 A lookups + 1 MX lookup + 1 NS lookup +
 5163: #   3x RDAP/WHOIS IP queries (up to 6 TCP connections) +
 5164: #   2 domain WHOIS TCP connections = up to 17 network operations.
 5165: #   Writes result hashref to $self->{_domain_info}{$domain} (cache).
 5166: #
 5167: # Notes:
 5168: #   Result is served from $self->{_domain_info}{$domain} on all
 5169: #   subsequent calls for the same domain within one parse_email() lifetime.
 5170: #   The cache is invalidated (reset to {}) by parse_email().
 5171: #
 5172: #   MX selection: the lowest-preference MX record is used (most preferred
 5173: #   server).  Only the primary MX is analysed; backup MXs are ignored.
 5174: #
 5175: #   NS selection: the first NS record returned by the resolver is used.
 5176: #   DNS resolvers do not guarantee a consistent ordering; the choice of
 5177: #   nameserver may vary between calls on different machines or at different
 5178: #   times.
 5179: #
 5180: #   MX and NS lookups are skipped entirely when Net::DNS is not installed.
 5181: #   In that case mx_*, ns_* keys are never present in the result.
 5182: #
 5183: #   WHOIS date fields (registered, expires) have time and timezone
 5184: #   components stripped by removing everything from the first 'T' or 'Z'
 5185: #   onward; the stored value is a plain YYYY-MM-DD string.  Parsing
 5186: #   uses the first matching pattern from a priority list; any fields not
 5187: #   found in the WHOIS response are absent from the result (not undef).
 5188: #
 5189: #   whois_raw is truncated to the first 2048 bytes of the raw WHOIS
 5190: #   response.  Structured fields (registrar, dates, abuse) are parsed from
 5191: #   the full response before truncation.
 5192: #
 5193: #   recently_registered is set to integer 1 when present; it is absent
 5194: #   (not 0) when the domain is not recently registered or when no creation
 5195: #   date was found.  The threshold is 180 days before time() at the moment
 5196: #   of analysis.
 5197: sub _analyse_domain {

 5373: # _parse_domain_whois_abuse( $domain ) -> hashref

 5422: sub _raw_whois {
 5423:     my ($self, $query, $server) = @_;
 5424:     $server //= 'whois.iana.org';
 5425:     $self->_debug("WHOIS $server -> $query");
 5426:     my $sock = eval {
 5427:         IO::Socket::INET->new(
 5428:             PeerAddr => $server,
 5429:             PeerPort => 43,
 5430:             Proto    => 'tcp',
 5431:             Timeout  => $self->{timeout},
 5432:         );
 5433:     };
 5434:     return undef unless $sock;
 5435:     print $sock "$query\r\n";
 5436:     my $response = '';
 5437:     eval {
 5438:         local $SIG{ALRM} = sub { die "timeout\n" };
 5439:         alarm($self->{timeout});
 5440:         while (my $line = <$sock>) { $response .= $line }
 5441:         alarm(0);
 5442:     };
 5443:     alarm(0);
 5444:     close $sock;
 5445:     return $response || undef;
 5446: }

 5684: 
 5685: =head1 AUTHOR
 5686: 
 5687: Nigel Horne, C<< <njh at nigelhorne.com> >>
 5688: 
 5689: =head1 ALGORITHM: DOMAIN INTELLIGENCE PIPELINE
 5690: 
 5691: For each unique non-infrastructure domain found in the email, the module
 5692: runs the following pipeline:
 5693: 
 5694:     Domain name
 5695:         |
 5696:         +-- A record  --> web hosting IP  --> RDAP --> org + abuse contact
 5697:         |
 5698:         +-- MX record --> mail server hostname --> A --> RDAP --> org + abuse
 5699:         |
 5700:         +-- NS record --> nameserver hostname  --> A --> RDAP --> org + abuse
 5701:         |
 5702:         +-- WHOIS (TLD whois server via IANA referral)
 5703:                +-- Registrar name + abuse contact
 5704:                +-- Creation date  (-> recently-registered flag if < 180 days)
 5705:                +-- Expiry date    (-> expires-soon or expired flags)
 5706: 
 5707: Domains are collected from:
 5708: 
 5709:     From:/Reply-To:/Sender:/Return-Path: headers
 5710:     DKIM-Signature: d=  (signing domain)
 5711:     List-Unsubscribe:   (ESP / bulk sender domain)
 5712:     Message-ID:         (often reveals real sending platform)
 5713:     mailto: links and bare addresses in the body
 5714: 
 5715: =head1 WHY WEB HOSTING != MAIL HOSTING != DNS HOSTING
 5716: 
 5717: A fraudster registering C<sminvestmentsupplychain.com> might:
 5718: 
 5719: =over 4
 5720: 
 5721: =item * Register the domain at GoDaddy (registrar)
 5722: 
 5723: =item * Point the NS records at Cloudflare (DNS/CDN)
 5724: 
 5725: =item * Have no web server at all (A record absent)
 5726: 
 5727: =item * Route the MX records to Google Workspace or similar
 5728: 
 5729: =back
 5730: 
 5731: Each of these parties has an abuse contact, and each can independently
 5732: take action to disrupt the spam/phishing operation.  The module reports
 5733: all of them separately.
 5734: 
 5735: =head1 RECENTLY-REGISTERED FLAG
 5736: 
 5737: Phishing domains are very commonly registered hours or days before the
 5738: spam run.  The module flags any domain whose WHOIS creation date is
 5739: less than 180 days ago with C<recently_registered =E<gt> 1>.
 5740: 
 5741: =head1 SEE ALSO
 5742: 
 5743: L<Net::DNS>, L<LWP::UserAgent>, L<HTML::LinkExtor>, L<MIME::QuotedPrint>,
 5744: L<ARIN RDAP|https://rdap.arin.net/>
 5745: 
 5746: =head1 REPOSITORY
 5747: 
 5748: L<https://github.com/nigelhorne/Email-Abuse-Investigator>
 5749: 
 5750: =head1 SUPPORT
 5751:
